class="nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-cGMI2b"><section class="DA9Qj nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-fmcmS-oXtfBe"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-c5RTEf"></div><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-qWD73c"><h5 class="cHE8Ub Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-qWD73c">Google Threat Intelligence Group </h5><p class="nRhiJb-qJTHM khCp7b"></p></div></section></div></section><div class="nRhiJb-DARUcf"><div class="nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-qWD73c-cGMI2b"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-ibL1re dzoHJ"><div class="aLW4J" track-metadata-module="left rail"><h5 class="qZDXV Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-wNfPc">Google Threat Intelligence</h5><p class="nRhiJb-cHYyed Mrfygc nRhiJb-BP2Omd-ma6Yeb-KE6vqe nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-cGMI2b">Visibility and context on the threats that matter most.</p><a class="nRhiJb-LgbsSe  nRhiJb-LgbsSe-OWXEXe-CNusmb-o6Shpd " href="https://cloud.google.com/security/products/threat-intelligence" track-metadata-module="left rail"track-metadata-module_headline="google threat intelligence" track-name="learn more"track-type="button"track-metadata-position="cta"track-metadata-eventdetail="cloud.google.com/security/products/threat-intelligence">Learn more </a></div></div><div class="OYL9D nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-OiUrBf" jsname="tx2NYc"><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Written by: Patrick Whitsell</p>
<hr></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Google Threat Intelligence Group’s (GTIG) mission is to protect Google’s billions of users and Google’s multitude of products and services. In late October 2024, GTIG discovered an exploited government website hosting malware being used to target multiple other government entities. The exploited site delivered a malware payload, which we have dubbed “TOUGHPROGRESS”, that took advantage of Google Calendar for command and control (C2). Misuse of cloud services for C2 is a technique that </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/apt29-evolving-diplomatic-phishing"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">many</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/china-based-threat"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">threat</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> </span><a href="https://www.eset.com/us/about/newsroom/press-releases/cyber-espionage-group-turla-new-campaign-uses-instagram-to-spy-on-its-targets/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">actors</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/tracking-apt29-phishing-campaigns"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">leverage</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> in order to blend in with legitimate activity. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">We assess with high confidence that this malware is being used by the PRC based actor </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/apt41-dual-espionage-and-cyber-crime-operation?e=48754805"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">APT41</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> (also tracked as HOODOO). APT41’s targets span the globe, including governments and organizations within the global shipping and logistics, media and entertainment, technology, and automotive sectors. </span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Overview</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In this blog post we analyze the malware delivery methods, technical details of the malware attack chain, discuss other recent APT41 activities, and share indicators of compromise (IOCs) to help security practitioners defend against similar attacks. We also detail how GTIG disrupted this campaign using custom detection signatures, shutting down attacker-controlled infrastructure, and protections added to Safe Browsing.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig1.max-1800x1800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig1.max-1800x1800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig1.max-1800x1800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig1.max-1800x1800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 1: TOUGHPROGRESS campaign overview</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Delivery</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT41 sent spear phishing emails containing a link to the ZIP archive hosted on the exploited government website. The archive contains an LNK file, masquerading as a PDF, and a directory. Within this directory we find what looks like seven JPG images of arthropods. When the payload is executed via the LNK, the LNK is deleted and replaced with a decoy PDF file that is displayed to the user indicating these species need to be declared for export. </span></p></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><pre><code>$ unzip -l 出境海關申報清單.zip
  Length      Date    Time    Name
---------  ---------- -----   ----
        0  2024-10-23 11:00   image/
    12633  2024-10-23 10:53   image/1.jpg
    10282  2024-10-23 10:54   image/2.jpg
     8288  2024-10-23 10:54   image/3.jpg
     4174  2024-10-23 10:54   image/4.jpg
   181656  2024-10-23 10:54   image/5.jpg
   997111  2024-10-23 11:00   image/6.jpg
   124928  2024-10-23 11:00   image/7.jpg
    88604  2024-10-23 11:03   申報物品清單.pdf.lnk
---------                     -------
  1427676                     9 files</code></pre></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The files “6.jpg” and “7.jpg” are fake images. The first file is actually an encrypted payload and is decrypted by the second file, which is a DLL file launched when the target clicks the LNK. </span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Malware Infection Chain</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">This malware has three distinct modules, deployed in series, each with a distinct function. Each module also implements stealth and evasion techniques, including memory-only payloads, encryption, compression, process hollowing, control flow obfuscation, and leveraging Google Calendar for C2.</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">PLUSDROP</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> - DLL to decrypt and execute the next stage in memory.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">PLUSINJECT</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> - Launches and performs process hollowing on a legitimate “svchost.exe” process, injecting the final payload.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">TOUGHPROGRESS</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> - Executes actions on the compromised Windows host. Uses Google Calendar for C2. </span></p>
</li>
</ol>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TOUGHPROGRESS Analysis</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TOUGHPROGRESS begins by using a hardcoded 16-byte XOR key to decrypt embedded shellcode stored in the sample’s “.pdata” region. The shellcode then decompresses a DLL in memory using </span><a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/ddi/ntifs/nf-ntifs-rtldecompressbuffer" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">COMPRESSION_FORMAT_LZNT1</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. This DLL layers multiple obfuscation techniques to obscure the control flow. </span></p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Register-based Indirect Calls</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Dynamic Address Arithmetic</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">64-bit register overflow</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Function Dispatch Table</span></p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The registered-based indirect call is used after dynamically calculating the address to store in the register. This calculation involves two or more hardcoded values that intentionally overflow the 64-bit register. Here is an example calling CreateThread.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig2.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig2.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig2.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig2.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 2: Register-based indirect call with dynamic address arithmetic and 64-bit overflow</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">We can reproduce how this works using Python “ctypes” to simulate 64-bit register arithmetic. Adding the two values together overflows the 64-bit address space and the result is the address of the function to be called.</span></p></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig3.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig3.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig3.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig3.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 3: Demonstration of 64-bit address overflow</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig4.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig4.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 4: CreateThread in Dispatch Table</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">These obfuscation techniques manifest as a Control Flow Obfuscation tactic. Due to the indirect calls and arithmetic operations, the disassembler cannot accurately recreate a control flow graph.</span></p>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Calendar C2</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TOUGHPROGRESS has the capability to read and write events with an attacker-controlled Google Calendar. Once executed, TOUGHPROGRESS creates a zero minute Calendar event at a hardcoded date, 2023-05-30, with data collected from the compromised host being encrypted and written in the Calendar event description. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The operator places encrypted commands in Calendar events on 2023-07-30 and 2023-07-31, which are predetermined dates also hardcoded into the malware. TOUGHPROGRESS then begins polling Calendar for these events. When an event is retrieved, the event description is decrypted and the command it contains is executed on the compromised host. Results from the command execution are encrypted and written back to another Calendar event.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In collaboration with the Mandiant FLARE team, GTIG reverse engineered the C2 encryption protocol leveraged by TOUGHPROGRESS. The malware uses a hardcoded 10-byte XOR key and generates a per-message 4-byte XOR key. </span></p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Compress message with </span><a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/openspecs/windows_protocols/ms-xca/5655f4a3-6ba4-489b-959f-e1f407c52f15" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">LZNT1</span></a></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Encrypt the message with a 4-byte XOR key</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Append the 4-byte key at the end of a message header (10 bytes total)</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Encrypt the header with the 10-byte XOR key</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Prepend the encrypted header to the front of the message</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The combined encrypted header and message is the Calendar event description</span></p>
</li>
</ol></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 5: TOUGHPROGRESS encryption routine for Calendar Event Descriptions</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/apt41-innovative-tactics-fig6.max-1700x1700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><p>Figure 6: Example of a Calendar event created by TOUGHPROGRESS</p></div></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><div jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="M0Q3Qb" class=" "><h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Disrupting Attackers to Protect Google, Our Users, and Our Customers</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GTIG’s goal is not just to monitor threats, but to counter and disrupt them. At Google, we aim to protect our users and customers at scale by proactively blocking malware campaigns across our products. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">To disrupt APT41 and TOUGHPROGRESS malware, we have developed custom fingerprints to identify and take down attacker-controlled Calendars. We have also terminated attacker-controlled Workspace projects, effectively dismantling the infrastructure that APT41 relied on for this campaign. Additionally, we updated file detections and added malicious domains and URLs to the Google Safe Browsing blocklist. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In partnership with Mandiant Consulting, GTIG notified the compromised organizations. We provided the notified organizations with a sample of TOUGHPROGRESS network traffic logs, and information about the threat actor, to aid with detection and incident response.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Protecting Against Ongoing Activity</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">GTIG has been actively monitoring and protecting against APT41’s attacks using Workspace apps for several years. This threat group is known for their creative malware campaigns, sometimes leveraging Workspace apps. </span></p>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Google Cloud’s Office of the CISO published the April 2023 </span><a href="https://services.google.com/fh/files/blogs/gcat_threathorizons_full_apr2023.pdf" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Threat Horizons Report</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> detailing HOODOO’s use of Google Sheets and Google Drive for malware C2.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In October 2024, </span><a href="https://www.proofpoint.com/us/blog/threat-insight/malware-must-not-be-named-suspected-espionage-campaign-delivers-voldemort" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Proofpoint published</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> a report attributing the VOLDEMORT malware family to APT41. </span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The DUSTTRAP malware family, </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/apt41-arisen-from-dust"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">reported by GTIG and Mandiant</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> in July of 2024, used Public Cloud hosting for C2.</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In each case, GTIG identified and terminated the attacker-controlled Workspace projects and infrastructure APT41 relied on for these campaigns.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Free Web Hosting Infrastructure</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Since at least August 2024, we have observed APT41 using free web hosting tools for distributing their malware. This includes VOLDEMORT, DUSTTRAP, TOUGHPROGRESS and likely other payloads as well. Links to these free hosting sites have been sent to hundreds of targets in a variety of geographic locations and industries. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT41 has used Cloudflare Worker subdomains the most frequently. However, we have also observed use of InfinityFree and TryCloudflare. The specific subdomains and URLs here have been observed in previous campaigns, but may no longer be in use by APT41.</span></p>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Cloudflare Workers</span></h3>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">word[.]msapp[.]workers[.]dev </span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">cloud[.]msapp[.]workers[.]dev </span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TryCloudflare</span></h3>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">term-restore-satisfied-hence[.]trycloudflare[.]com</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">ways-sms-pmc-shareholders[.]trycloudflare[.]com</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">InfinityFree</span></h3>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">resource[.]infinityfreeapp[.]com</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">pubs[.]infinityfreeapp[.]com</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT41 has also been observed using URL shorteners in their phishing messages. The shortened URL redirects to their malware hosted on free hosting app subdomains. </span></p>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">https[:]//lihi[.]cc/6dekU</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">https[:]//tinyurl[.]com/hycev3y7</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">https[:]//my5353[.]com/nWyTf</span></p>
</li>

<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">https[:]//reurl[.]cc/WNr2Xy</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> </span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">All domains and URLs in this blog post have been added to the Safe Browsing blocklist. This enables a warning on site access and prevents users from downloading the malware. </span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Indicators of Compromise</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The IOCs in this blog post are also available as a <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/d9dd10452ab3d30217dce44408c6b21a06309132e9ec7935a0798e07c8c3bf29" rel="noopener" target="_blank">collection</a> in Google Threat Intelligence.</span></p>

The exploited site delivered a malware payload, which we have dubbed “TOUGHPROGRESS”, that took advantage of Google Calendar for command and control (C2). APT41’s targets span the globe, including governments and organizations within the global shipping and logistics, media and entertainment, technology, and automotive sectors. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eOverview\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn this blog post we analyze the malware delivery methods, technical details of the malware attack chain, discuss other recent APT41 activities, and share indicators of compromise (IOCs) to help security practitioners defend against similar attacks. The shellcode then decompresses a DLL in memory using \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-hardware/drivers/ddi/ntifs/nf-ntifs-rtldecompressbuffer\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eCOMPRESSION_FORMAT_LZNT1\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e. This DLL layers multiple obfuscation techniques to obscure the control flow. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eRegister-based Indirect Calls\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eDynamic Address Arithmetic\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e64-bit register overflow\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eFunction Dispatch Table\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThe registered-based indirect call is used after dynamically calculating the address to store in the register. Once executed, TOUGHPROGRESS creates a zero minute Calendar event at a hardcoded date, 2023-05-30, with data collected from the compromised host being encrypted and written in the Calendar event description. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThe operator places encrypted commands in Calendar events on 2023-07-30 and 2023-07-31, which are predetermined dates also hardcoded into the malware. style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eDisrupting Attackers to Protect Google, Our Users, and Our Customers\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eGTIG’s goal is not just to monitor threats, but to counter and disrupt them. At Google, we aim to protect our users and customers at scale by proactively blocking malware campaigns across our products. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eTo disrupt APT41 and TOUGHPROGRESS malware, we have developed custom fingerprints to identify and take down attacker-controlled Calendars. We have also terminated attacker-controlled Workspace projects, effectively dismantling the infrastructure that APT41 relied on for this campaign. Additionally, we updated file detections and added malicious domains and URLs to the Google Safe Browsing blocklist. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn partnership with Mandiant Consulting, GTIG notified the compromised organizations. We provided the notified organizations with a sample of TOUGHPROGRESS network traffic logs, and information about the threat actor, to aid with detection and incident response.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eProtecting Against Ongoing Activity\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eGTIG has been actively monitoring and protecting against APT41’s attacks using Workspace apps for several years. This threat group is known for their creative malware campaigns, sometimes leveraging Workspace apps. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eGoogle Cloud’s Office of the CISO published the April 2023 \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://services.google.com/fh/files/blogs/gcat_threathorizons_full_apr2023.pdf\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThreat Horizons Report\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e detailing HOODOO’s use of Google Sheets and Google Drive for malware C2.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn October 2024, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.proofpoint.com/us/blog/threat-insight/malware-must-not-be-named-suspected-espionage-campaign-delivers-voldemort\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eProofpoint published\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e a report attributing the VOLDEMORT malware family to APT41. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThe DUSTTRAP malware family, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/apt41-arisen-from-dust\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ereported by GTIG and Mandiant\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e in July of 2024, used Public Cloud hosting for C2.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn each case, GTIG identified and terminated the attacker-controlled Workspace projects and infrastructure APT41 relied on for these campaigns.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eFree Web Hosting Infrastructure\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSince at least August 2024, we have observed APT41 using free web hosting tools for distributing their malware. This includes VOLDEMORT, DUSTTRAP, TOUGHPROGRESS and likely other payloads as well. Links to these free hosting sites have been sent to hundreds of targets in a variety of geographic locations and industries. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAPT41 has used Cloudflare Worker subdomains the most frequently. However, we have also observed use of InfinityFree and TryCloudflare. The specific subdomains and URLs here have been observed in previous campaigns, but may no longer be in use by APT41.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3\u003e\u003cspan
